        "courseDescription": "<p>As of 2007, for the first time in human history, more than half the world&rsquo;s peoples lived in cities. It is estimated that by 2030 over 60% will be urban-dwellers. This demographic shift suggests that for many (if not most) people, their primary encounter with &ldquo;nature&rdquo; will be urban based. This course explores the idea of &ldquo;urban-nature&rdquo; by 1) focusing on the ways in which various theorists have challenged traditional ways of viewing both &ldquo;the city&rdquo; and &ldquo;nature&rdquo; and 2) encouraging students to develop their own critical perspectives through ethnographic engagements with the city of Toronto. <\/p>",

        "code": "ANT462H1",
        "courseDescription": "<p>This course examines how anthropologists have studied the way that people hope, imagine, love, and despise. Ethnography of the intimate realms of affect raises important questions about knowledge production and methodology as well as offering insight into how people come to act upon the world and what the human consequences of such action are. The course will also examine how the intimate is socially produced and harnessed in the service of politics and culture. Topics will include grief and its lack; dreams and activism; love and social change; memory and imperialism; sexuality and care; and violence and hope.<\/p>",
